thee face thou hast put prison without hurt dooing vnto therefore thou traytour theefe mahound thou cursed thou art worthy sit seate royall therefore arise vp mee e thee sit therewith hee drew god pleased said ah noble king oberon pray thee seeing god pleased put away thy displeasure pardon breaking thy commaundement haue sore punished pray thee displeased spake hasty worde prison famine caused doe breaking thy commaundement confesse ill therein yet negligence forgetting ala sir remember courtesie ye shewed yee found wood gaue rich horne cup often time haue succoured therefore sir require thee pardon trespass helpe need see well without ye grace god helpe nothing saue life thus besought god pardon giue grace destroy enemy horrible behould made prayer came sarazin huon said sir marriners thought haue ledde vnto kinge iuoryn mombrance cannot tell taken shee daughter admirall gaudise mahound take soule knewe certaine king iuoryn might haue damsell hee would haue burnt hath shewed cause death father admirall gaudise brother king iuoryn hee vncle damsell aduertised ten marriners would haue deliuered hand vncle iuoryn tooke slew would deliuer entreatie thus haue wedded damsell iuoryn heard made mee war heere citie puissance hath slayne men led away beast prouision hath burnt destroyed countrey euerie day commeth ouerrunnes country hath young man know countrey hee last day hee slewe nephewe mine whome right dearely loued called sorbryn hee sonne sister whome haue sorrowe heart cannot appeased hath led away horse called blanchardyn best horse ten realmes like world wherefore desire may deserue seruice abide mee doe much might haue saide younge man taken prisoner horse againe restored doe shall reward shall alwaies rich companie sir quoth gerames hee come hether shewe mee shall doe best bring horse also vnto freend quoth admirall shew courtesie shall abandon realme bee pleasure commaundement word old gerames yssued ship companie entred citie anfalerne admirall galaffer came pallaice gerames sayd sir companie require shewe v damsell whose sake maintaine war freend quoth admirall young man would shew vnto see well bee olde ancient wherefore young ladie set thinge admirall tooke gerames hand led chamber whereas escleremond assoone ladie saw gerames knew wherewith began chang colour fell swound chamber making great outcrie admirall galaffer saw right sorrowfull said faire ladie doe make sorrow troubled sight olde man haue brought hether nay surely sir quoth shee paine hath taken mee right side whereby haue often time great annoyance sir pleasure would gladly speak french knight customably know many thing peradueture may shew thing shalbe health frenchman right discreet giuing good counsell madame quoth admirall pleaseth well speake secretly ladie called gerames said freend pray thee giue good counsaile may eased paine endure madame quoth gerames honour admirall heere present shall ayd wise shalbe eased paine endure gerames subtill well perceiued mind ladie approached neere vnto sat downe together couch gerames quoth ladie pray aduenture hath brought hether madame quoth wee bee come hether reason tempest sea ladie quoth pray become huon faith quoth beleeue hee dead departed v maruelous tempest rose sea shippe perished ship drowned broken small peeces except huon saued v table wood wherevpon arriued isle neere v wee land came vnto v ten marriners tooke thence huon blindfold hand foot fast bound power releeue himselfe ten marriners brought hether admirall galaffer hath slayn al therefore thinke surely huon dead iesus haue mercie vppon thus heere admirall hath assured wed mee yet neuer medled bodily haue made beleeue made vowe mahound twoo yeares come man haue vse body loue huon whome cannot forget admirall hath beleeued long liue shall neuer forget huon shall alwayes ready die payn keepe bodily company man liuing ah sir gerames might doe much might escape hence great courtesie might escape hence come christian realme would yeeld selfe abbie nunnes entent reasidue life might pray soule louer huon madam quoth gerames dismayed escape hence whatsoeuer come thereof shall carie admirall came vnto sayd freend hold ouerlong talking damsell come away haue taried long ynough gerames departed escleremond strayning hand admirall galaffer tooke gerames arme brought hall supper supper communed feates warre historie twoo dayes king iuoryn made course anfalerne huon came vnto iuoryn sayd sir cause men armed let v goe visite admirall galaffer man warre ought neuer lye still vntill hath brought enemie vtter ruine seemeth setteth little keepeth still neece hee subiect one holdeth land freend quoth iuoryn say truely shall doe counsaile made cryed citie euerie man make readie go king anfalerne huon desirous haue battaile armed tooke blanchardyn good horse mounted without stirrop tooke great speare hand good sharpe head time huon pallaice king iuorins daughter leaning window chamber accompanied diuers lady damsel shee beheld huon shee said mahound goodly sight behould yonder young man sitting horse blanchardyn well becommeth armour goodlier man cannot found hardie last day slew sorbryn valiantest knight pagany also wanne good horse yet displeased whe played chesse hardy embrace kisse would haue loued wise required loue would haue refused though father sworne contrarie hundred time thus lady damsel deuised together huon set little thereby thus king iuoryn men issued citie mombrance came field roade foorth toward anfalerne last came gate citie ordered battaile array huon great desire attaine renowne came gate speare hand cried alowd walles said galaffer lord goe shew come iust hath slaine nephew serue like sort may meete battaile else shall deliuer faire escleremond galaffer neere heard huon saide knew well reason horse blanchardyn whereof right sorowfull said gerames friend shal shew heere hath done al ill shall see yee keepe promise sir quoth gerames take care faith owe god shall render horse man doe pleasure gerames yssued armed well horsed tooke good speare hand hee goodly knight age puissant bodie time greatly redoubted horse hee stretched himselfe saddle wise stirrops stretched long handfull greatly praysed paynim saw admirall galaffer commaunded euery man armed himselfe armed richly gate opened gerames first issued company without citie strake horse spurres great space companie speare hand shield necke white beard hanging downe brest vnder helmet nowe huon part saw gerames comming hee spurred blanchardyn came gerames met together without word offer mee pray vnto god hee may reward huon quoth admirall seeing haue wife hold wel excused pray shew vnto cause wife case christian prince hardie trouble doe displeasure sir quoth huon came countrey left citie bourdeaux besieged emperour almaine hath taken citie slaine men hee keepeth seruage wife put prison kept great pouertie miserie remember sorrowe greefe sore gripeth heart member ioynts tremble displeasure huon quoth admirall pray leaue sorrow displeasure cast take ioy comfort holy law haue receiued shall ayde succour emperour hath done vnto many displeasure shall make warre whether dammage losse haue receiued shall constraine make full restitution shall lead company number people valley mountaines shall couered sir quoth huon courtesie succour offer humbly thanke please lord sauiour iesus christ hath ayded mee many peril hope aide mee shall neede make warre destroy christian bloud sir first shall goe holy sepulchre returne countrey doe get wife daunger paine shee sir wife haue wedded daughter admirall gaudise held babilon realme egipt huon shewed matter came faire escleremond whereof admirall sore abashed great maruailes hee hadde heard huon declare heard said one another without huon beene well beloued lord iesus christ hee could neuer haue escaped death one least aduentures shewed vnto admirall sir quoth huon emperour almaine hath taken citie wife destroyed men hath taken handes land signiories grace god shal doe much get againe cannot attaine thereto shall returne againe vnto haue succour ayd huon quoth admirall put melancholy giue mee knowledge cannot haue wil emperour shall bring people innumerable christendome shall tremble feare shall render vnto wife al land signiories men bee prison seruage shall put emperour hand doe pleasure else shal leaue land neither citie towne standing vppon earth sir quoth huon thanke heartily sir must woorke another way first escaped gulfe persia promised vnto god went mine owne countrey goe visite holy sepulchre ierusalem make warre vppon sarazins made warre vppon christian men sir may get emperour faire speach landes wife shall serue heart long liue shall make warre christian man may haue right reason shewed vnto mee sir quoth admirall say giue good thankes grace god shall goe voyage holy sepulchre take mee fiftie thousand men make warre paynim sarazins beleeue god shall put paine power exalt encrease lawe lord iesus christ sir quoth huon haue sayde nobly thus doe great grace glorie perpetuall shall deserue whereby shalbe crowned aboue emperiall heauen nowe leaue wee speake matter chap cxviii p howe admirall persia assembled much people hee huon armie tooke sea came port citie angory whereas found great number paynim sarazins readie defend port admirall huon deuised together many thinges admirall sent letter breefes commaunding throughout persia medium men warre bee readie gaue day bee readie goe certifying nauie shippes readie transporting done euerie man came day assigned meane season huon barnard went oftentimes together visited citie thauris whereas much honour made vnto whereof huon barnard oftentimes thanked god good aduenture sent thus yee haue heard admirall persia assembled great number people made readie entred shippe diuers shippes shipped armour horse huon desired please admirall tooke owne little shippe discharged tooke precious stone put another ship admirall deliuered serue sayd vnto admirall sir know well little ship came hether serue warres therefore sir doe giue vnto whereof admirall great ioy world none beautie rich huon gaue admirall bushell stone vnto lordes together thanked huon courtesie large stone kept owne vse three hundred gaue away residue hee entred shippe appointed euerie man entred shipps well fournished victualed war admirall tooke leaue daughter pitifully wept father departing weighed vp anchor hoysed vp sayles good winde anon farre port goodly sight beholde nauie departing made great noyse trumpet drummes horne sea ring thereof great ioy gladnesse huon barnard grace god sent longe sayled good winde sayle entred great sea caspis saw farre faire city standing seaside called citie angory wherein dwelt admirall right puissant rich time one tower pallaice saw perceiued puissant nauie come sayling fast towardes citie hee great maruaile sore dismayed abashed knewe well shippes persia penons banner hee sawe wauing vppon shippes vpon part sawe toppes forecastle baners standing white therein red cross said vnto lordes sir greatly dismayed abashed meaneth yonder great fleete seeing citie wonne reignard montauban lord fraunce called reignard montauban hee made bee christened eight yeares wonne againe vpon christian men admiral sonne admirall lord thereof wonne againe bee paynim sarazins may see vpon seaside readie abide v defend port sir quoth huon ought greatly thanke lord iesus christ faire aduenture see v enemy christian faith grace lord sauiour iesus christ day shall doe much citie inhabitant therein shall handes vse pleasure sir quoth admirall beseech almightie god giue v grace may great grace lord god shall doe vnto v wee may winne citie admirall caused men bee armed sawe halfe league citie port hauen kept defended admirall angory would yssue farre citie vntill hee sawe countenance christian men would make admirall persia huon aduanced themselues forward cast anchor launched boat well garnished men archer crosbowes landed port sauegard without danger shippes drew land vnshipped armour horse euerie man landed except assigned keepe shippes euerie man mounted vpon horse ordained three battailes first led huon twentie thousand men hautie hye courage second ledde great lord persia marshall hoast third guided admirall persia road ranke ranke admonishing men doe endeauours valiantly soft pace drewe battaile array towards citie chap cxix p howe admirall huon tooke port fought admirall angory dicomfited tooke citie howe afterward huon went desert abillant search aduentures admirall angory sawe perceiued christian men hadde taken land readie giue battaile comming towardes citie hee ordained ranged battailes deuided foure part set led guided hee thought best aduaunced forward number fiftie thousand men twoo hoastes sawe none feared death day faire cleare approached rush partes dashed together wise reason pouder dust rise horse sunne faire bright waxed darke shot partes flewe fast thicke though snowed first meeting many speares broken many knight borne earth could neuer releeued lay ground among horse feete died dolour many horse running abroad trayling bridle master lying dead vppon earth bloud myre great slaughter made vppon part huon went breaking great preasses whereas hee slewe many paynim euerie man feared saw admirall angoryes nephew slaine christian knight ranne fiercely paynim brake speare vppon huon huon fayled gaue maruailous great stroake speare passed bodie fell downe earth died huon ranne another gaue maruailous stroake passed sheeld bodie drawing speare hee fell earth neuer releeued three foure hee serued like manner valiantly behaue himselfe slewe eight speare brake drew sword therewith hee deedes fearfull behold hee cut legges armes rassed helmet none enemy durst approach neere vnto fledde birde doth hauke hee brake asunder thicke preasses hee bee feared enemy left hee neuer strooke man full stroake hee receiued slaine also barnard coozen euer followed maruailes armes hee sharpe eager knight also admirall angory enforced himselfe doe dammage vnto christian men hee sawe admirall persia slaying men came ranne admirall persia sawe encountred force puissance bare earth quickly releeued themselues sword hand willing slay beene done indeede men come succoured thether came many part twoo admiral hadde power one touch great force came thether paynim sarazins christian men could remount vp againe admirall persia faine fight foote hadde beene great ieopardie danger huon barnard come rescued came thether hastily heard showting cry made admirall persia brake asunder great preasse paynim saw huon approach neere vnto sore afraid knewe well parted spread abroad durst abide huon seeing admirall persia foot among enemy sword valiantly defending himselfe little auailed beene quickly succoured huon sawe hee sayde oh right puissant admirall haue doubt huon tooke speare handes paynim hee slaine therewith ranne admirall angory gaue horrible vehement stroake speare passed bodie foote hee fell downe dead among men whereof paynim sore dismayed abashed saw lord lye dead vppon earth huon quickly tooke admiral horse raine bridle aduenture vppon euening huon alone stood leaning ouer shippe board beholding sea plaine peaceable hee remembred duchesse escleremond wife therewith teares ran tenderly downe visage said ah right noble ladie remember peril daunger left pouertie miserie bee nowe haue ioynt member tremblesh displeasure feare least false emperour cause die ere returne beganne make great sorrow greefe barnard farre said ah sir knowe well fortune aduentures haue come vnto god hath ayded saued perill death therefore take good comfort selfe laud praise lord god sendeth vnto doubt haue perfect hope trust ayd comfort neuer forgetteth good heart serue thus wordes barnard comforted huon admirall came leaned huon deuised together diuers sundrie matter time arose vp wind tempest great horrible sayles broken diuers place mastes brake flew ouer board shippe sea beganne bee rough furious euerie man thought haue beene perished fortune tempest horrible euerie man deuoutly called vpon lord god saue perill daunger sir marriners sir pray may bee let v drawe quarter sir quoth huon mee thinkes sore dismayed ash lord made semblance shall neuer haue ioy heart vntill knowe enemie causeth perish fast way shall neuer rest hee right sorrowfull sore displeased searched day find man woman al vaine sawe sunne went rest could find creature sore discomforted chose tree vnder layd downe slept morning saw sunne rise beames thereof went vpward heauen made fume went downeward sawe slewe murdered brother abell wherefore great sinne haue committed damned bee suffer martirdome within tunne wherein closed burning serpent toad heere within deuouring mee yet cannot die heere shall bee vntill day iudgement paine shall doubled haue shewed thee thy demaund wherefore repute thee foole thou art hardy enter desert whereas neuer man entred departed without death know troth hether repaireth twoo enemy feends hell shall slay thee beare thy soule hell without thou wilt doe shall shew thee freend quoth huon pray thee shew thou speakest thing thou wilt doe doe entent may depart hence nothing world shall doe thee thou wilt shewe mee way howe may depart hence freend quoth cain shall shewe thee thou shalt doe thou shalt take mall iron thou seest strike therewith long vppon tunne vntill thou hast broken entent may yssue deliuered shall set thee sauegard ierusalem france countrey soeuer thou wilt wish thou wilt doe haue sayd deliuer torment shall set thee wheresoeuer thou wilt land christian heathen thou doest haue saide night shall cause thee die great tormentes anon thou shalt see come hether two diuels hell foule hideous behold shall stangle thee beare thy soule hell ah good lorde quoth huon humbly require beseech thee saue mee torment cain quoth huon thou speakest mee faire sayest thou list deliuer thee tunne vntill first thou shewest mee may depart hence cain sayd thou wilt promise mee thy faith thy part paradice deliuer mee tunne shall shewe thee manner howe thou shalt escape hence cain quoth huon haue doubt promise thee keepe faith thou wilt shew mee manner howe may depart desert shall deliuer thee thy torment cain said thou shalt goe little path thou seest heere vppon thy right hand shall bring thee straight seaside farre hence goe downe mountaine whereas thou shalt find shippe therein one man thou doest enter shippe blesse three time hee thou shalt finde feende hell shewe vnto howe thou art cain escaped rowling tun bid passe thee ouer say thou wilt goe slay christian men bee world bring soules hell hee heareth thee say thus hee wlil passe thee ouer safetie longe since hee hath taried mee thinketh escape tun thou must take thee mall yron vpon thy necke entent hee shall better beleeue thee surely passe thee ouer cain quoth huon pray thee troth thou hast sayd freend quoth cain lye neuer word pray thee seeing haue shewed thee manner thou mayest escape take mall yron breake asunder tunne may deliuered paine torment cain quoth huon pray thee shew mee hee put thee tun name sir quoth cain know troth god heauen set heere displeased slaying brother abell wherefore haue suffered much paine sorow cannot endure therefore yet againe pray thee deliuer mee hence cain quoth huon god forbid deliuer thee seeing lord god hath set thee know troth thou shalt neuer depart thence except bee commaundement thou shalt bee euer mee rather bee periured vndoe thing god haue done punish thee euils thou hast done knowe well euill haue done breaking promise thee god lightly pardon mee abide thou thy cursed sinnes sure mee thou shalt haue none ayd chap cxxi p huon departed cain passed sea vessell guided diuell beleeued beene cain huon arriued citie called colander whereas found admirall persia barnard cozen layde siege citie cain well vnderstood huon said ah thou false traytor beguiled mocked thou art worthy beleeued thinge thou sayest thou lyest worse dogge oh thou false periured traitour thou hast ill kept thy promise thou art worthy bee beleeued cain quoth huon good gettest thou none mee thou art worthie bee heard thou hast staine thy deare brother false enuie cursed treason whereof thou art full goe thy way false traytour much euill cannot bee done vnto thee bee content tunne thou art thou needest feare refreshing furthering mee well hast thou deserued within short time thou shalt haue worse paine sorrow ah traytour quoth cain false lyer thou hast lost thy part paradice thou lyest quoth huon vnto thee ought bee kept neither faith promise thou hast slaine abell thy brother wherefore thou art punished well hast thou deserued ah thou false lier quoth cain subtilly thou hast deceiued mocked mee thy false word subtilties see well thou wilt goe hence leaue still paine certainly quoth huon promised thee beguile thee mee thou shalt come without hee commaund set thee heere well huon quoth cain know certaine thy life thou wert neuer better counsailed thou haddest deliuered incontinent would haue strangled thee ah false feend quoth huon yet hast thou repentaunce taken traytour brohart shee declared vnto theeues caused put cloathes put rich apparell sawe apparelled thought ladie damsell world could passe beautie shee come againe beautie thought selfe well therefore mine aduice wee send vnto noble ambassage desiring come citie roome say citie shall doe obeysance better send betimes late intent neither none doe dammage landes roome agreed saying sent receiued ambassadours right honourably came roome whereas receiued lord peaceably entred roome went mette great ioy brought city trumpet drummes blowing vntill came church saint peter hee offered prooue vertue paynim rested horse squier mounted rested vntill came nise euening late hee arriued without perceiuing siege tent little hadde beene gate great skirmish wherefore sarazins wearie trauaile also part croissant arriued sarazins lodged hee came gate prayed porter let enter porter saw two person hee christian hee suffered enter without refuse croissant sawe hee without danger ioyfull came one best lodging towne alighted supped host late goe night court tarried night vntill next morning hee went pallace whereas found earle remon deuising lordes knight deedes warre croissant saluted earle lordes earle saw young man greatly beheld thought life neuer seen goodly person thought hee come noble lineage tooke croissant hand demaunded name sir quoth name croissant croissant thirtie thousand men warre twentie thousand haue alreadie within towne considering hye courage come hether serue mee shall doe honour haue made knight shall giue banner beare doe thinkes doe paine shall lost sir quoth croissant god giue grace morrow may doe seruice may bee wealth christendome god may performe wanteth make knight dayes life shalbe earle incontinent sent son knight diuers whome made knightes croissant said croissant freend pray lord god giue fortune morrowe may vanquish battaile sir quoth god giue grace render thankes honour doe grace god morrow shall doe enemy shall curse houre came hether assaile while ye croissant thus made knight earles sonne others time came thether duke callaber hee came pallaice cheere made brother earle remon make mention thereof came season new knightes made quintaine sette vp prooue themselues duke callaber earle remon brother went thether verie desirous see best duke demanded earle yong knight road nephew hee thought neuer saw goodly yong person puissant age earle sayd come thether seeke honour hee lineage knew thus talked together young knight croissant came place whereas quintaine dressed vp earles sonne ranne brake speare peeces others assayed themselues brake speares fell earth force stroake none could remooue quintaine croissant saw assaied themselues ouerthrow quintaine great speare ran fiercely hee strake quintaine ouerthrew ground whereof euerie man great maruaile duke sayd earle neuer saw goodly stroake sayd greatly bee doubted giue stroakes hee greatly praised lady damsel present especially earles daughter hath slaine son ought greatly laud praise mahomet may bee reuenged vpon thee couched speare strake croissant middest sheeld speare flew peeces stroake croissant remooued though striken stone wall alighted vppon horse necke strake necke cleane asunder sort force king tumbled earth sore astonied stroke receiued quickly rescued croissant striken head sarazins remounted againe king ran croissant cast dart iauelins haue slain durst approch neere much feared howbeit hurt diuers place hee held sword handes wherewith hee strake man full stroake hee claue head braines hee sawe great admirall thicke preasse anone made way sarazins would faine haue raised vp againe banner could sarazins saw king dead banner lying ground courage beganne faile brayed opened array began loose place croissant tooke heed nothing slay great captaines last sawe kinge belmarin slaine many christian man day croissant gaue stroake right shoulder arme sheeld fell earth reason great dolour king felt fel aswound among horse feete whereas died miserably duke callaber earle remon regarding hye deedes armes done atchieued croissant hadde great maruell force puissance blessed houre hee borne thanking god comming thether rested beheld made enemy fly away none hardy abide finally shoulde rehearse hye deedes croissant day would ouerlong declare great prowesse paynim sarazins vtterly discomfited happie could saue well vnderstood earle remon hee sayd sir courtesie rich guiftes offer mee refuse thanke hartely thereof daughter offer giue trust shall doe honour vpon head shall set crowne gold make empresse rome whereas shall serued honoured ladie ouer countrey earle heard answeare croissant verie ioyfull sonne present neere hand rage displeasure sayd inragedly god croissant since thus shall bee disenherited earle made great cheere supper readie satte downe seruice make rehearsall supped diuers sport shewed hall houre requisite came euerie man went bed earle remon prepared croissant faire chamber rich bed companion sharpe weapon hand approached croissant bed earles sonne lifted vp sword str ke croissant stroake helmet sword swarned hand whereby perceiued hee armed hee warning comming whereof right neuer afraid life thought haue fled away croissant gaue stroake head sword claue chin fell downe dead slaine croissant squier whereof hee sorrie hee ran like man desperate much within short space slaine fiue fledde away another chamber durst speake one word chap clxxviii p howe croissant depated nise sword hand howe earle r mon sorrowfull death sonne chased croissant could bee found croissant saw himselfe enterprized hee slaine earles sonne great feare hee knewe wel taken danger life therefore hastely departed pallaice hee came stable horse stood found great yron chaine dore horse bee taken night time saw sore discomforted sayd oh good lord thy grace ayd ought well sorrie must leaue horse ala cannot tell mine armour certainely except god succour mee see way escape aliue ala thought haue beene married earles daughter farre haue slaine brother minded haue returned countrey soone vntill conquered landes whereby might haue beene receiued honourably sette nothing hee began sore weepe went towne might coulde trauaile long armour hee beheld voide house corner streete hee went thether vnarmed armour except sword white iacket rested vntill hee came gate called porter desired open gate saying businesse doe little without towne porter answeared stubbornely sayd rrquireth hast hee might well abide sayd hee would open gate vntill faire day freend quoth croissant pray thee shew courtesie porter answered fiercely sayd thou doest loose thy labour gate shall opened vntill sunne rise croissant saw porter would open gate faire meanes hee sette hand sword sayd thou false traitour except thou doest open ye gate incontinent sword shall slay thee porter saw croissant held naked sword hand strike great feare came forth hast keyes hande sayd sir shall open gate good howbeit afraide bread went lay old pallaice vpon burden strawe croissant saw departed towne nise alone afoo e hee made complaint lord god requiring humbly haue pitie hee went foorth trauailed three day three night without meat drinke little bread water hunger thirst could scarce sustaine himselfe foot last little sunne set hee came little towne called florencolle whereof gate shutte came thether subburbs hee saw house like tauerne hee sware though slaine would goe house eate drinke pay well shot better haue passed great perill life yee shall heare thus hee approached house heard cooke busie kitchin sawe great fire chamber greatest ruffian player dice towne prepared flesh fish supper croissant saw preparation made sixe ruffian entred house saluted host demaunded might lodged host sayd yea hee well serued wine meat wold demaund croissant went ruffian met sayd hee welcome pinched wincked one eye sayd softly master great trauailer come well point depart shall pay shot expences anon put dice hand whereby shal leaue gowne cappe monney haue croissant vnderstand spake whisperingly croissant sayd sir eate paying shot shall turne displeasure freend quoth maister pleaseth well eate v washed together sate downe table neere fier well serued euery thing croissant set hee began feede well hunger great three dayes eaten nothing bread water therefore hee better appetite also hee found good wine fresh dranke thereof pleasure well eaten drunke well chafed reason good wine host rose vp sayd sir time make reckoning euerie man pay part maister ruffian sayde sir make account doe better shew v wee shall pay euerie man alike sir quoth host neere reckon yee must pay twelue shilling looke euerie man pay part master ruffian began sweare bloud wound play dice see pay hee sayd croissant freend must come play v behold heere three dice good square wee must doe one must pay whole expences depart sir quoth croissant shall neede play dice know shall pay shot pay together without strife sayd well content therewith thanked one falsest villayne among wilfully cast downe potte wine vpon table whereof fellowes blamed answeared sayd sir need angry therewith none drinke thereof better haue fresh pot wine new vessell sayd well true host brought new pot full wine sayd sir potte wine first reckoning potte newe account maister ruffian sayd croissant sir take cast dice first cast shalbe croissant beheld fiercely sayd nay sir keepe mee neuer played dice life content twelue shilling shall pay shot reason longe voyage haue made well fournished monney haue thirteen shilling purse maister sayd thou art done bigge mightie neuer sawe mine eye man better made fourmed fledde away sword hand yonder hye way sir god sake come neere hee seemeth man hee angrie hee like man wittes without feare doubt magistrate commaunded follow horsebacke afoote ranne armour though captaine greatly afraide yet hee would bee first go foorth loued better another shold take aduantage thus side horsebacke afoote followed croissant kept high way far night also many would chafe themselues ouer much seeke wold make preasse receiue offering feared finde sought long space field high wayes could finde returned towne croissant went euer townward sword naked hand hee sawe two league entred high way praised god hee escaped without daunger hee sore displeased neuer penny purse nothing sword coat rich purse guirdle also sawe winter frost snow also felt cold winde much ill thus hee went foorth night next day vntill neere night arriued village faine sell sword lacke monney pay shot came lodge serued euerie thing would haue morning departed sold purse much hee could get hee trauailed long hee approached roome hee came lodging without gate lodged night morning demaunded host whome towne appertained lord thereof name gouerned towne host sayd freend hee nowe lord heere named guymart puille hee came hether young lord fairest young gentleman euer seene sonne noble emperour ide somewhat resemble ill rule full folly rich wealth father left hee spent gaue away euerie man would craue thing end hee left himselfe nothing liue heard say himselfe shame departed priuily squier went seeke aduentures man knoweth whether euer come againe communaltie cittie made little thereof hee departed sent king guymart puille whome haue made emperour empire croissant vnderstood host complained right pitiously himselfe sayde ala poore caitiffe shall thus haue lost al mine inheritance without recouerie besides haue nothing spend haue trade liue must behooue die hunger cold haue fiue twentie shilling sould purse thus well could continued till lent season began somewhat hotter euerie day morning would heare seruice euerie man saw beheld greatly ye great beautie diuers knew would make semblance thereof intent wold giue nothing sawe would shun way know many hee done much good vnto giuen wise become rich poore none would offer one morsell bread whereof sorrowfull sawe well monney gone neuer penny left thought sell gowne rather die hunger sould eight twentie shilling taried lodging long money endured hee continued vntill easter time monney gone thought would goe streetes see might espie burgess whome done time past good vnto demaund courtesie yssued lodging walked streetes saw rich burgesse leaning window house croissant knew well hee made rich poore thought acknowledge himselfe burgesse croissant went saluted right humbly sayd sir haue remembrance poore caitiffe whome fortune contrarie time past much good serued bee good man beleeue goodnes haue remembrance may doe shall fare better burgesse heard croissant beheld fiercely knew presently without making manner answeare called page commaunded bring pan full water windowe master commanded burgesse tooke pan full water beheld croissant stood vnder window cast water vppon head faire haire coat shirt wet croissant without word speaking made himselfe cleane afterward said burges liued long offence done deerely buy burgesse proud disdainfull set little word croissant right sorrowfull tooke way towards pallaice ye old pallaice whereas man dwelled long space entred gate great stood open saw great piller whereas lay two burden strawe layd downe slept right sorrowfull angrie burgesse wet water burges cast water vppon croissant hee went pallaice emperour guymart flatter please found emperor leaning window saluted sayd made member hee seemeth like champion readie fight euer saw man life follow counsaile strike head cast pit may neuer memorie liue long may doe dammage put empire hould appertaine emperour guymart vnderstoode burges beheld fiercely sayd speake matter thou doest like traytor thou knowest well deed thou bee made rich thou art like betrayed lord iesus christ therefore command thee hencefoorth come culpable almighty god sinne haue done hold honour signiorie reason ought appertaine day easter day vpon day euerie good christian man ought humble himselfe god cry mercie pardon sinnes reason make thus emperour guymart complained himselfe went downe pallaice walked vp downe himselfe olde pallaice neere pallaice looked gate saw man lye sleeping burden straw thought incontinent croissant report
